# R Code block for simulating the random normal experiment

``` r
# Creating an empty dataframe as a dummy, Jamovi already has a empty dataframe named 'data' by default
data <- data.frame(matrix(NA, nrow = 10000, ncol = 1))
```

``` r
# sample mean and SD values for the normal simulation 
set.seed(1442) 

mu <- 3.86         # mean of ER_AVG 
sigma <- 0.739     # SD of ER_AVG 
n <- 10000         # simulation number 

# The rnorm() function generates 'n' random values from a normal distribution 
simulated_data <- rnorm(n = n, mean = mu, sd = sigma) 
data$Simulation <- simulated_data 

# Sort the data in the ascending order 
data$Sorted_Simulation <- sort(data$Simulation) 
print(data) 
```

# R-Code block for simulating the Central Limit Theorem

``` r
# Loading the 'dplyr' and library for data manipulation. 
library(dplyr) 
```

    ## Warning: package 'dplyr' was built under R version 4.4.3

    ## 
    ## Attaching package: 'dplyr'

    ## The following objects are masked from 'package:stats':
    ## 
    ##     filter, lag

    ## The following objects are masked from 'package:base':
    ## 
    ##     intersect, setdiff, setequal, union

``` r
# Set a seed for reproducibility. 
set.seed(1442) 

# Let's define discrete uniform distribution parameters for simulation. 
# We are starting with a uniform population of integers from 1 to 10. 
# The theoretical population mean for a uniform distribution is (a+b)/2, so (1+10)/2 = 5.5 
# And the population standard deviation is sqrt(((b-a+1)^2 - 1) / 12), so sqrt(((10-1+1)^2-1)/12) = 2.872 
num_samples <- 1000      # simulation count 

# Generating 5 columns of uniform random data and store them directly in the data tab. 
data$Sample1 <- sample(1:10, size = num_samples, replace = TRUE) 
data$Sample2 <- sample(1:10, size = num_samples, replace = TRUE) 
data$Sample3 <- sample(1:10, size = num_samples, replace = TRUE) 
data$Sample4 <- sample(1:10, size = num_samples, replace = TRUE) 
data$Sample5 <- sample(1:10, size = num_samples, replace = TRUE) 

# Creating a new column to compute the row-wise mean of the 5 samples. 
data$Sample_Mean <- rowMeans(data[, c("Sample1", "Sample2", "Sample3", "Sample4", "Sample5")]) 
print(head(data,20))
```
